  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_33017068-3ef7-465a-b7ed-f208c5fa9731'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText15315133235214366485" style="display:none">Kaylin Neya is a Hawk, part of the elite force tasked with keeping the City of Elantra safe. Her past is dark, her magic uncontrolled and her allies unpredictable. And nothing has prepared her for what is coming, when the charlatans on Elani Street suddenly grow powerful, the Oracles are thrown into an uproar and the skies rain blood.<br /><br />The powerful of Elantra believe that the mysterious markings on Kaylin's skin hold the answer, and they are not averse to using her - however they have to - in order to discover what it is.<br /><br />Something is coming, breaking through the barriers between the worlds. But is it a threat that Kaylin needs to defend her city against - or has she been chosen for another reason entirely?</span>

<div id="review_120363766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120363766" />
    <a title="Felicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/666892-felicia"><img alt="Felicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437521850p2/666892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120363766?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felicia" href="/user/show/666892-felicia">Felicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=vaginal-fantasy">vaginal-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120363766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14777028989261712582">GUYS...I hate to be negative, but the last few books in this series have not lived up to my immense excitement for them. I feel like what I personally loved about this series is not what the AUTHOR likes about it, is that weird/arrogant/ridiculous to say? It's a really weird place to be, because I feel like a jerk not loving what the author's vision is, because she's the the OWNER of the series, but I'm reading these books going, "WHERE ARE THE CHARACTERS AND PLOT I WANT TO SEE?! WHERE ARE YOU G</span>
  <span id="freeText14777028989261712582" style="display:none">GUYS...I hate to be negative, but the last few books in this series have not lived up to my immense excitement for them. I feel like what I personally loved about this series is not what the AUTHOR likes about it, is that weird/arrogant/ridiculous to say? It's a really weird place to be, because I feel like a jerk not loving what the author's vision is, because she's the the OWNER of the series, but I'm reading these books going, "WHERE ARE THE CHARACTERS AND PLOT I WANT TO SEE?! WHERE ARE YOU GOING, NOOOOOO!"<br /><br />For this series, it's the Nightshade factor I'm really frustrated about. I'm a huge Nightshade fan and I think she hates Nightshade. It's kinda like Lillith Saintcrow's Dante series, where she obviously HATED Jaf after the first few, and killed me with where it went, haha. I mean, it's her vision, but I don't have to love it, you know? I can APPRECIATE it, but emotionally I wasn't on track, and that's how I feel with this book and series as a whole. Why am I writing so much about it? Because I love these worlds and the characters. But...Severn? THERE"S NOTHING THERE! AND THINGS ARE STILL TOO CONFUSING!<br /><br />Ok, I'm gonna go read some comics and calm down, hahaha.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1776234825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1776234825?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Dimitrova" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova">Maria Dimitrova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=tbr-clean-up-2017">tbr-clean-up-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776234825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18227555223566810985">This series is either getting better or I've finally reached the point of addiction where I no longer notice the aggravating parts. <br/><br/>I can't say much without resorting to constant spoiler tags. However I can say that things got pretty tense for a while and for a while I was worried that this time around Kaylin's blind luck won't save her. I know, I know there are more instalments so she can't die but I was still worried that she won't be the same after. And I've grown fond of that bumbling idiot </span>
  <span id="freeText18227555223566810985" style="display:none">This series is either getting better or I've finally reached the point of addiction where I no longer notice the aggravating parts. <br /><br />I can't say much without resorting to constant spoiler tags. However I can say that things got pretty tense for a while and for a while I was worried that this time around Kaylin's blind luck won't save her. I know, I know there are more instalments so she can't die but I was still worried that she won't be the same after. And I've grown fond of that bumbling idiot *affectionate smile* She's even showing signs of improvement now that she's forced to confront her abilities. <br /><br />There seems (to me at least) that there's a love triangle forming between Severn, Nightshade and Kaylin. Or at least that both males are interested in Kaylin. She's however blind to it (or at least pretending not to notice though I'm more inclined to believe she's totally ignorant). It's endearing to me since I'm the same in RL. <br /><br />The Arcane and the other Dragon Lords remain my top favorite characters and I can't wait for Kayling to start her etiquette lessons for two reasons - it promises to be hilarious and absolutely aggravating for the poor soul (dragon) that is to be her teacher (he shows a lot of promise!) and so we can finally meet the Dragon Emperor. Though it's very likely that Kaylin's new teacher will eat her long before she gets to meet the Emperor :D<br /><br />There are some new developments in Elantra and I can't wait to see what's next in store for the Chosen and her city!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18227555223566810985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11362044487274660478" style="display:none">I feel like I liked this one better than the previous one because it was less of a constant info dump, but due to life, it took me a month to finish this &amp; I can't remember much of the beginning at this point. <br /><br />The plot of this better, it had a driving end point &amp; more dragons. Maybe extra annoying about choosing strangers over people she knows. Time away from the book and the last half of the story, she finally wasn't annoying. <br /><br />Will I read more? Yeah, I have low expectations and these fit that. </span>

<div id="review_119398375" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119398375" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209300-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549484486p2/4209300.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119398375?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/4209300-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209300-mark?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119398375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3414394769211024194">I adore Michelle Sagara. <br/> <br/>It's true, I do adore her. And I am in awe of how deep her creativity is. There is not one book of hers that I have read and thought 'oh, that's just like [insert author/book:]'. For me, with Michelle, it just it doesn't happen, and while I certainly haven't read everything out there - and tend to avoid those deemed 'classics' in the genre - I have read a lot. <br/> <br/>Michelle is one of those writers whose work makes me stop all of my own work so I can just immerse myself in s</span>
  <span id="freeText3414394769211024194" style="display:none">I adore Michelle Sagara. <br /> <br />It's true, I do adore her. And I am in awe of how deep her creativity is. There is not one book of hers that I have read and thought 'oh, that's just like [insert author/book:]'. For me, with Michelle, it just it doesn't happen, and while I certainly haven't read everything out there - and tend to avoid those deemed 'classics' in the genre - I have read a lot. <br /> <br />Michelle is one of those writers whose work makes me stop all of my own work so I can just immerse myself in story and wallow! <br /> <br />Why do I like it so much? Agh! It is actually hard for me to pin point. <br /> <br />I admire writers who have a masterful grasp of worldbuilding (and you will hear me go on and on about this in future reviews), so yep, she ticks that box. <br /> <br />I have to be interested by the character(s) and, to a degree, empathise with them (if I am truly going to rave about a book), and she has always managed to do that. <br /> <br />And mostly I have to be believe the words a writer writes. Terry Dowling calls this 'Voice of Truth' and when you've got it, you've got it. Michelle has it. Her writing is evocative and powerful, machiavelian and heartfelt. <br /> <br />But to talk about 'Cast in Chaos'... where to begin without offering any spoilers? <br /> <br />There aren't any big battles in this book. Personally I don't care, I am not one for battle scenes so the lack of them doesn't make me think twice. But that doesn't mean that this is a slow book (for battle scenes - despite popular opinion do not make a story travel faster [unless you skim read them:]). The story is packed with menace and sense of urgency, as well as humour and humanity, and it places another piece of the story arc firmly into place - heading us towards a confrontation with the Shadows. <br /> <br />There is more talking in this book. But I like the 'talking'. And Kaylin is maturing before our eyes. When we began Book One, Kaylin was very frustrating and always opening her mouth to speak the first words that popped into her head. By Book Six you actually notice that she is biting her tongue alot to stop from putting her foot in her mouth. The character has grown before our eyes and it's so gradually done that you while you notice it has happened you can't say exactly where this bit of 'growing up' has occured. And what more can you ask of any book but that it takes you on a journey with the characters, especially a character who is dynamically changed by the experiences that you experience with her.<br /><br />Cast In Chaos is a brilliant tale of redemption and forgiveness, unexpectedly deep discusions and humourous interludes. It explores the nature of language and its limitations and human blindness as well as generosity. It is an awesome piece of entertainment with characters you will come to love, who you will cheer for and cry for, rage at and laugh with (and at). It is a story of human flaws, and heroism despite itself. <br /> <br />My only criticism is that the books are too short. And I don't just say that because I want to read more - and boy do I ever! - but because although Michelle crafts each story to stand alone, they all tie in together within a larger story arc, and that arc is epic. Steven Erikson epic. And I have to have more. <br /> <br />I have to! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3414394769211024194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_112911499" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112911499" />
    <a title="ambyr" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2670408-ambyr"><img alt="ambyr" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451339945p2/2670408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112911499?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambyr" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambyr" href="/user/show/2670408-ambyr">ambyr</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=acquired%E3%85%A1borrowed">acquiredㅡborrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=author%E3%85%A1female">authorㅡfemale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=protagonist%E3%85%A1female">protagonistㅡfemale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=author%E3%85%A1poc">authorㅡpoc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2670408-ambyr?shelf=genre%E3%85%A1fantasy%E3%85%A1secondary-world">genreㅡfantasyㅡsecondary-world</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112911499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3719130626831150816">I am calling this The Cast Book In Which People Finally Answer Each Other's Questions. Not that there's not still plenty of evasiveness and need-to-know, but an astonishing number of queries (at least, for this series) actually elicit responses, sometimes even more detailed than Kaylin wants. It made for a much more satisfying read, and helped build a stronger picture of the world.<br/><br/>Metaphysical endings, in which rather than kill X bad guy or deliver Y plot token the protagonist must in some mysti</span>
  <span id="freeText3719130626831150816" style="display:none">I am calling this The Cast Book In Which People Finally Answer Each Other's Questions. Not that there's not still plenty of evasiveness and need-to-know, but an astonishing number of queries (at least, for this series) actually elicit responses, sometimes even more detailed than Kaylin wants. It made for a much more satisfying read, and helped build a stronger picture of the world.<br /><br />Metaphysical endings, in which rather than kill X bad guy or deliver Y plot token the protagonist must in some mystical fashion rewrite the laws of the universe, seem to be all the rage in books I'm reading lately. <i>Who Fears Death</i> had one. So did <i>The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</i>. I found the later more satisfying than the former, but both ultimately left me feeling like I'd either missed something, or they'd been insufficiently set up. <br /><br /><i>Chaos</i> follows a similar path--but in contrast, by the time I reached the final critical pages I felt like I understood what was going on, and that it had been well telegraphed from the start. (At least, I understood what was going on as well as Kaylin did, which is perhaps setting a low bar.) Some of that is because Sagara had five previous books to worldbuild, of course, but given how sparse the exposition was previously, this volume had to carry a lot of weight. And it does so while still maintaining a pretty brisk pace.<br /><br />In fact, if there's one thing I regret about the book, it's that the plot is paced quickly enough that we don't get much time for secondary character development. The Arkon makes a fairly strong showing, and the other dragons to a lesser extent, but Teela and Tain are almost entirely absent and the Hawklord never appears on page. As for Nightshade and Severn--well, the good news is both romantic plotlines experience some movement. In any other series it would be so tiny as to be unnoticeable, but for the Cast books they qualify as gigantic leaps. The bad news is that Severn in particular gets no real development as an individual. He's still almost as much a cipher as he was in book one.<br /><br />(Frankly, I'd be just as happy if the romantic plotlines continue not to move. Both Nightshade and Severn make me twitch as romantic partners for Kaylin. If I had to pick a pairing, I. . .think I would vote for Kaylin/Teela. Because why the hell not?)<br /><br />All of this makes it sound like I didn't enjoy the book. But I did! The worldbuilding is great fun, and Kaylin's haplessness manages to be endearing. Not my favorite Cast book--that'd be Courtlight--but probably tied for second place with Fury. I look forward to the next one.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3719130626831150816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_83012519" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83012519" />
    <a title="CJ - It&#39;s only a Paper Moon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1357098-cj---it-s-only-a-paper-moon"><img alt="CJ - It&#39;s only a Paper Moon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437680885p2/1357098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83012519?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CJ - It&#39;s only a Paper Moon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CJ - It&#39;s only a Paper Moon" href="/user/show/1357098-cj---it-s-only-a-paper-moon">CJ - It&#39;s only a Paper Moon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1357098-cj---it-s-only-a-paper-moon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1357098-cj---it-s-only-a-paper-moon?shelf=out-of-the-ordinary">out-of-the-ordinary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1357098-cj---it-s-only-a-paper-moon?shelf=women-detectives">women-detectives</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer83012519&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83012519" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12510272441973435058">This installment is just as heartwrenching as any of the others. There are too many things to actually go on about so I'll just pick a few.<br/><br/>The theme of this book seemed to be about Home and Trust. How the two are connected and what it means to be without both and then find your way back.<br/><br/>The story of the Devourer and the Elemental Garden, toward the end of the book, seems to mirror the relationship of Severn and Kaylin. It's clear that Severn is in love with her (at least to me) and he goes on at</span>
  <span id="freeText12510272441973435058" style="display:none">This installment is just as heartwrenching as any of the others. There are too many things to actually go on about so I'll just pick a few.<br /><br />The theme of this book seemed to be about Home and Trust. How the two are connected and what it means to be without both and then find your way back.<br /><br />The story of the Devourer and the Elemental Garden, toward the end of the book, seems to mirror the relationship of Severn and Kaylin. It's clear that Severn is in love with her (at least to me) and he goes on at one point, in order to save her, to let her know why he loves her. Of course he doesn't say that he's 'in love with her' but I think that with the two of them, they don't need to. When the question is brought up in passing, Kaylin can't answer why she loves Severn - she's too afraid - but she can talk about why she trusts him, which seems to be more important.<br /><br />The Devourer has lost much and in the path of his wreckage, in the pursuit of finding that which he has lost, he receives a second chance and is brought back to his maker/punisher/lover the four elements. Much like Severn, who lives with the choice of killing Steffi &amp; Jade - an act that should have been done by Kaylin - everyday and is forced to live with the fact that the person he loves is hurting and partly sculpted by his actions, I would imagine, is nothing short of torture. <br /><br />As for Kaylin, she is still angry (who wouldn't be) but she is also angry with herself. Love is thrown around in as a concept but never exchanged between any of the characters. Making certain scenes a bit sterile and a little stunted.<br /><br />The fact that Nightshade kisses Kaylin made my eyebrow raise for two reasons. Kaylin seems to so asexual at this point that it is hard for me to think of her with anyone and secondly, I want her to eventually be with Severn! Which would be hard but everything in life worth having is.<br /><br />However, a Nightshade interlude would be quite interesting.<br /><br />The dreaded Emperor meeting may be happening soon and I can only hope that Kaylin grows up just a little bit more so that she is confident in herself as well as her abilities.<br /><br />How come Severn doesn't have a possible love interest? Why is everyone so celibate?!<br /><br />Sorry that was a random thought. Anyhoo, it was nice to see Tiamaris and Ybelline (sp). Can't wait for the next installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12510272441973435058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110278728" />
    <a title="Estara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3590834-estara"><img alt="Estara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271356174p2/3590834.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110278728?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Estara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Estara" href="/user/show/3590834-estara">Estara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781426864148" href="/book/show/8728342-cast-in-chaos">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Estara by: </span>
      auto-buy author
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590834-estara?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590834-estara?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590834-estara?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590834-estara?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer110278728&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110278728" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2904067822566185981">I really appreciate Kaylin growing up in the year that has taken place since the first book timeline. She really needs it for this particular crisis and I loved the resolution of why there are magic words on her body and what a Chosen actually is.<br/> <br/>There is still more to see, we haven't seen the Emperor yet and we haven't dealt with the Outcaste or the situation with Nightshade for that matter, but I did have the feeling of a major climax with this particular end-of-the-world situation and especi</span>
  <span id="freeText2904067822566185981" style="display:none">I really appreciate Kaylin growing up in the year that has taken place since the first book timeline. She really needs it for this particular crisis and I loved the resolution of why there are magic words on her body and what a Chosen actually is.<br /> <br />There is still more to see, we haven't seen the Emperor yet and we haven't dealt with the Outcaste or the situation with Nightshade for that matter, but I did have the feeling of a major climax with this particular end-of-the-world situation and especially with addressing a lot of the background tension with Severn. Considering he rarely speaks about his emotions, the fact that he had to speak up this time was totally believable in the context of the development here.<br /><br />I think it's the strongest entry in the series so far.<br />_______________<br />A delight to read more closely the second time and learn even more about the make-up of the fief of Tiamaris and the Elemental Garden. I will ever be in team Severn.<br />_________<br />On my third reread I keep wondering why we haven't seen more of the Maker since and what is happening with the fact that the Nurannor have a Chosen, too. I mean stuff keeps happening to Kaylin and he's simply the pathfinder for his people?? But then maybe it is because she's the current Chosen of the original world... hmm. A bit like the idea behind the Fionnavar Tapestry of Guy Gavriel Kay, who is Canadian, too ^^ - like MSW.<br /><br />Other than that I was more sensitized toward Severn and Kaylin's interaction in the last book and here, where he gives her an anchor that is deeply necessary (not that Nightshade's saving her from the paths between the worlds isn't a great scene, too - but I still think it has to do with the power he eventually wants her to use on his behalf and not with her as a person, no matter how he likes to play with fire aka flirt with her), and shows a lot more than we have seen of his feelings apart from the horrible explanation for what happened to Jade and Steffi.</span>

<div id="review_112798277" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112798277" />
    <a title="Keziah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2351024-keziah"><img alt="Keziah" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112798277?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keziah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keziah" href="/user/show/2351024-keziah">Keziah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2351024-keziah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2351024-keziah?shelf=epic-world-building">epic-world-building</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2351024-keziah?shelf=genre-epic-fantasy">genre-epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2351024-keziah?shelf=theme-magical-beings">theme-magical-beings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2351024-keziah?shelf=theme-magic">theme-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2351024-keziah?shelf=protagonist-leos">protagonist-leos</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2351024-keziah?shelf=protagonist-magic-user">protagonist-magic-user</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2351024-keziah?shelf=protagonist-female">protagonist-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2351024-keziah?shelf=blog-post">blog-post</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112798277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9833063894312588190">Although it doesn't seem possible, Sagara just keeps getting better and better with the <i>Elantra</i> series. I think <i>Cast in Shadow</i> remains my favourite <i>Elantra</i> novel, but <i>Cast in Chaos</i> has stolen the second favourite prize from <i>Cast in Fury</i>.<br/><br/>Sagara's writing is just one of the things I love about these novels. There is such a moreish air to the story. I didn't stay up until after midnight just because my best friend wanted to read the book today. I couldn't stop reading. Every word flowed onto the ne</span>
  <span id="freeText9833063894312588190" style="display:none">Although it doesn't seem possible, Sagara just keeps getting better and better with the <i>Elantra</i> series. I think <i>Cast in Shadow</i> remains my favourite <i>Elantra</i> novel, but <i>Cast in Chaos</i> has stolen the second favourite prize from <i>Cast in Fury</i>.<br /><br />Sagara's writing is just one of the things I love about these novels. There is such a moreish air to the story. I didn't stay up until after midnight just because my best friend wanted to read the book today. I couldn't stop reading. Every word flowed onto the next and I found myself sitting up almost holding my breath as the story reach the climax. My favourite aspect of the <i>Elantra</i> series however is the growth of the heroine Kaylin. Each book has really taught Kaylin an important lesson, although the focus of the book has not really been the lesson, aside from <i>Cast in Shadow</i>. With each novel Kaylin becomes more and more three dimensional and her foibles and weaknesses come to light.<br /><br />It's not only Kaylin who shines in this book, although she certainly does dominate the story more than usual. Tiamaris and Tara make an appearance, along with Sanabalis and the Arkon, and of course Severn and the rest of the Hawks. The confrontation with Nightshade over the events of the previous book doesn't lead where I expected it to, but did open up a whole lot more questions regarding Kaylin past and the mystery of the runes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9833063894312588190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_561176158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/561176158" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/561176158?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8698700-cast-in-chaos">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=i-own-this">i-own-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer561176158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5259555669213981788">First read 8 March 2013.<br/><br/>Sixth in the Chronicles of Elantra fantasy series for young adults about a remarkable young woman who has a lot of learning to endure yet.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>This particular story is about the elements that make up the world: earth, air, fire, and water. Being a magical world, it seems an element may well be missing, creating an opportunity to build a story around refugees fleeing their homeland and how a civilized country/world would meet their plight. A story that is made up of word</span>
  <span id="freeText5259555669213981788" style="display:none">First read 8 March 2013.<br /><br />Sixth in the Chronicles of Elantra fantasy series for young adults about a remarkable young woman who has a lot of learning to endure yet.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />This particular story is about the elements that make up the world: earth, air, fire, and water. Being a magical world, it seems an element may well be missing, creating an opportunity to build a story around refugees fleeing their homeland and how a civilized country/world would meet their plight. A story that is made up of words, and words are very, very important to Dragons, to the Devourer, to Tara, to the Barrani. And, in the end, to Kaylin.<br /><br />I just can't help liking Kaylin. She doesn't care what grief may rain down upon her head; it's people who are important to her. She'll do whatever it takes to make them safe.<br /><br />Crack me up, it's the first time Severn has mentioned that Kaylin needs to draw up a budget. And the window at HQ is acting up! It's getting downright chatty to <em>every</em>one.<br /><br />Ooh, I hate that Sagara left us hanging without Lady Alyssa's reaction at the end of the story. After all the fuss she kicked up, I wanted to watch!<br /><br />Oh, I cried...Severn finally tells Kaylin what he thinks and feels. And Kaylin is growing up.<br /><br />Whoa, it really <em>is</em> an emergency! The Dragons have invited the Barrani High Lord and his Lady to the Imperial Palace!! We also get more tidbits about the Barrani. <br /><br />After the way in which everyone emphasizes the emperor's will and autonomy, why they should imagine that Kaylin would believe she had the right to barge in? Still, she does like to take that walk on the wild side, and <em>Cast in Chaos</em> definitely provides lots of opportunities for Kaylin to walk.<br /><br />Oh, yeah, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8679140-cast-in-ruin" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Ruin in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Ruin</em>
</a>, 7, oughta be fascinating after Kaylin's run-ins with Lord Diarmat!<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />Evarraon's elemental garden is upset. Again. It feels wrong, not as alive, and when Kaylin leaves it, she falls out of the world only to be chased by the Devourer. <br /><br />That's not the worst of Kaylin's worries however. She has been assigned a tutor for those etiquette lessons she's been avoiding. <em>Wait'll she finds out who it is! She won't be able to blow this one off!</em><br /><br />Still, magic is erupting and becoming stronger throughout Elantra, enough that it threatens their world. Thank the gods that Kaylin bears the marks of the Chosen.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Private Lord Kaylin Neya</strong> of the Hawks is always in the...hmmm...do I dare say right place at the right time? She may fulfill this role for the world, but I'm sure others are beginning to see her as a harbinger of doom, LOL. As for her partner in the Hawks, <strong>Corporal Lord Severn Handred</strong> has gone from mortal enemy to necessary friend.<br /><br /><strong>Lord Tiamaris</strong>, a Dragon, is now the fieflord of the former Barren fief with <strong>Tara</strong>, the Tower, the Avatar, the Lady, more of a partner than a mere building who raises questions and provides answers. And Tara is growing in her understanding of people. Of life. <strong>Morse</strong> (she killed Barren in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304351-cast-in-silence" target="_blank" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in SIlence in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Silence</em>
</a>, 5) is now Tiamaris' second-in-command.<br /><br /><strong>Lord Sanabalis</strong> is one of four Dragon lords at the Imperial Court and is becoming a friend to Kaylin. There are also Dragon <strong>Lords Emmerian</strong> and <strong>Diarmat</strong>, a very fussy, punctilious, UNfriendly Dragon who is Captain of the Imperial Guard---he still thinks he should be able to eat people who offend him. The <strong>Arkon</strong> is the oldest Dragon at court, and he hasn't left the palace library in thousands of years. The <strong>Dragon Emperor</strong> is anxious to meet Kaylin, but not so anxious that he will see her before she passes her etiquette lessons. Seems he's not very tolerant, nor does he have a sense of humor, and there is a very real possibility that he will eat Kaylin on sight if she is in any way rude. <em>Yup, that on-sight bit is a real possibility...this</em> is <em>Kaylin we're talkin' about!</em><br /><br /><strong>Evanton</strong> is the Keeper of an elemental garden on Elani street. A garden that is in wild disarray and trying to relay a message. <strong>Grethan</strong> is his defective Tha'alani apprentice (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/641910.Cast_In_Secret" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Secret in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Secret</em>
</a>, 3). <strong>Margot Hemming</strong> is a sort of fraudulent seer who ticks off <strong>Lady Alyssa</strong> whose father, <strong>Garavan Larienne</strong>, is the Chancellor of the Exchequer. <br /><br /><em>The Hawks include:</em><br />The Hawks are one of three peacekeeping forces in Elantra, and <strong>Lord Grammayre</strong> is the Hawklord. Think of them as the investigators of the threesome. <strong>Sergeant Marcus Kassan</strong>, a.k.a., Ironjaw, a Leontine, is back and in charge. <strong>Caitlin</strong> is his unofficial second-in-command and a human. <strong>Teela</strong> and <strong>Tain</strong> are Barrani who much prefer the streets to the Barrani High Court. Both are friends of Kaylin's. <strong>Tanner</strong> is human and enjoys a laugh at Kaylin's expense.<br /><br /><strong>Ybelline Rabon'alani</strong> is the Emperor's Tha'alani, the castelord of her people with the most experience of how humans think, and Kaylin's friend. Her efforts with Everly may provide a way to communicate with the newcomers/invaders. <strong>Scoros</strong> is a founding teacher and <strong>Draalzyn</strong> is the Tha'alani who serves in Missing Persons. <br /><br />The <strong>High Lord</strong>, the castelord of the Barrani, the former Lord of the Green, and his <strong>Consort</strong>, the Lady, require Lord Kaylin's help. And they're not too happy with her stance. <br /><br /><strong>Lord Sabrai</strong> is an oracle and in charge of the Oracular Halls. <strong>Sigrenne</strong> is a guard and very like Marrin in her care of the oracles in the Halls. After past experience with Kaylin, she's comfortable with her. <strong>Everly</strong> is an oracle who communicates through his painting. <strong>Marya</strong> is a a midwife who frequently calls Kaylin in for help. Although, the grief Marya experiences in this story is not likely to be something Kaylin can fix.<br /><br />Turns out that <strong>Lord Nightshade</strong>, an outcaste Barrani fieflord (whose true name is Calarnenne), acknowledges that events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304351-cast-in-silence" target="_blank" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in SIlence in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Silence</em>
</a>, 5, caused him to seek his opportunity, take it, and explore while he awaited Kaylin's arrival, for she is part of the <em>Regalia</em>, a story of the Barrani. <strong>Lord Andellen</strong> is the Barrani guard who has become a part of Kaylin's life. <br /><br /><strong>Vakillirae</strong> chooses to sacrifice himself for knowledge and to give his people time to flee, which his friend, <strong>Enkerrikas</strong>, records. <strong>Effaron</strong> is the traveler able to speak to Kaylin; he's leading the others on their journey. <strong>Merjah</strong> leads the refugees.<br /><br />The other two peackeeping forces are the <strong>Swords</strong> who act as patrolmen and riot police and the <strong>Wolves</strong> are black ops, always in the shadows, tracking down wrongdoers.<br /><br /> The <strong>Aerians</strong> are birdmen, but not shifters. <strong>Barrani</strong> are the upper class in this society, although not the uppermost. The <strong>Leontine</strong> are lion shifters. <strong>Arcanists</strong> are mages who work independently of the Dragon Emperor. The <strong>fiefs</strong> in this story---Tiamaris, Nightshade, and <em>Ravellon</em>---are only three out of seven criminal neighborhoods around Elantra. The beings who rule fiefs are the <strong>fieflords</strong> who provide the name of the fief itself.<br /> <br /><b>The Cover</b><br />The cover is brilliant greens and oranges highlighting and surrounding Kaylin and those changing tattoos on her arms as she stands, facing us, with her arms outstretched, and her long dark hair blowing in the draft.<br /><br />The title reflects the state of mind of the citizens of Elantra---<em>Cast in Chaos</em>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5259555669213981788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_817786714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/817786714" />
    <a title="S.E." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6181827-s-e"><img alt="S.E." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584603462p2/6181827.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/817786714?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.E." class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.E." href="/user/show/6181827-s-e">S.E.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer817786714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16631383787905468857">I read the first few books of this series many years ago and did not go on because the library did not have the newer books in stock. Recently, I re-read them to fully appreciate the whole package before moving on...<br/><br/>I like this series. Undoubtedly, the world-building and character development are nothing short of great. It is easy to get immersed in the whole make-believe Elantran world with Kaylin as she explored, stumbled around and fought her way through all the mysteries and daunting challen</span>
  <span id="freeText16631383787905468857" style="display:none">I read the first few books of this series many years ago and did not go on because the library did not have the newer books in stock. Recently, I re-read them to fully appreciate the whole package before moving on...<br /><br />I like this series. Undoubtedly, the world-building and character development are nothing short of great. It is easy to get immersed in the whole make-believe Elantran world with Kaylin as she explored, stumbled around and fought her way through all the mysteries and daunting challenges. The books are confidently and intelligently written - the author’s storytelling remain tight, her descriptions vivid, the tone and narrative voice strong and sure. <br /><br />However, as I move on from Book 3, I find myself less and less enthusiastic. <br />1) Maybe it’s because the story revolved around the Leontines in “Cast in Fury”. Of all the races in this Elantran world, I like the Leontines the least. They’re so hot-tempered and easily flustered (note again title of book 4) that just reading a chapter about how they handle their affairs can be kind of exhausting. <br />2) Unlike the Harry Dresden series or many other such series where you have to read the books in chronological order for fear of missing significant developments in the whole plot, there is nothing much to miss in the Elantran Chronicles if you skip one book in between, especially book 4. While I appreciate the author’s in-depth analysis of Kaylin’s psyche in any given crisis, as well as the detailed narration of almost every situation so you feel like you are there every step of the way, sometimes too many details can be as intimidating as info-dumping. And such a writing style gives rise to a series that is big on plot but slow in build-up and severely lacking in action. Major advances should really be made plotwise. <br />3) Romance. Hmm... what romance? There’s the unspoken love between her and Severn (which is expressed in Book 6 but done so matter-so-factly), hints of physical attraction between her and Nightshade, but looking for romance in the 6 books is like looking for the proverbial needle in the haystack. I expect so much more from a female author...<br /><br />I think I have listed enough grouses. I may not have fairly judged the series because, in all honesty, I enjoyed reading all the books. I still want to read on, but not because the plotlines are oh-so-exciting, but because there are still many loose ends lying around, and because the conclusion (if there is one) is still worth chasing after. And of course, I have not given up hope searching for the ever-elusive romance …<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16631383787905468857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_77470170" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77470170" />
    <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship"><img alt="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297107033p2/2109885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77470170?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship">Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=dtb">dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=i-heart-the-cover-art">i-heart-the-cover-art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=series-abandoned">series-abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=magic-users">magic-users</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=bye-bye">bye-bye</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77470170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11900425351712457926">I was a bit shocked at the thickness of this book, I had hopes it was going to be a wildly interesting ride. Sadly I was almost as disappointed with this one as I was the last. <br/><br/>Mostly, it was just too long, repetitive with some utterly useless paragraphs. I was tempted to get a red pen out and start crossing out the unnecessary parts. I especially grew tired of Kaylin repeating what she'd done or learned to everyone she encountered sometimes in greater detail than was needed.<br/><br/>However, there were </span>
  <span id="freeText11900425351712457926" style="display:none">I was a bit shocked at the thickness of this book, I had hopes it was going to be a wildly interesting ride. Sadly I was almost as disappointed with this one as I was the last. <br /><br />Mostly, it was just too long, repetitive with some utterly useless paragraphs. I was tempted to get a red pen out and start crossing out the unnecessary parts. I especially grew tired of Kaylin repeating what she'd done or learned to everyone she encountered sometimes in greater detail than was needed.<br /><br />However, there were a few things that peeked my interest which saved this from a two star rating. The blatant introduction to possible romance. So far in this series there's been none whatsoever. Kaylin's had a hard life and has showed no interest in love, sex or having her own children despite how much she loves them. We all knew Nightshade was interested in her but she's always remained reluctant. He finally makes a move and she reacts badly. <br /><br />When Severn makes hints about his feelings, I'm relieved as I've been waiting for this for a while now, and when he explains his reasons for loving Kaylin and she acknowledges this it gave me hope. At the same time I grew worried that the status quo would remain in place despite their love for one another. I'm not sure Kaylin can handle it which is why Severn has said nothing for so long.<br /><br />Parts of the plot were of interest to me, especially the origins of humans and the new race of people who've found their home within Tiamaris's fief. I look forward to reading about their progress and how the other races react to their presence/existence. <br /><br />I am surprised Sagara hasn't done a book on the Aerians yet and that Kaylin hasn't got much closer to meeting the Dragon Emperor. I know that she desperately needs to learn self-preservation around those that can devour her but I hardly think etiquette lessons with a stuffy dragon will help matters. Besides she does pretty well with the Arkon and he's no picnic either. I really hope <i>Cast in Ruins</i> makes for a better read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11900425351712457926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2451520417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4226354874058964613"><strong>Couldn't Put it Down</strong><br/><br/>*****Spoilers*****<br/><br/>What an amazing tale! Watching Kaylin grow is fantastic, her interactions with the world and people in it is always a surprise. So much happens in this book, it's hard to focus on a few things but Everly and his paintings have become a source of fact when the Oracular Halls are not well respected, the child is. I hope as he grows, they're able to balance his physical needs with the absorption caused by his art by way of his visions.<br/><br/>Marcus has taken a back se</span>
  <span id="freeText4226354874058964613" style="display:none"><strong>Couldn't Put it Down</strong><br /><br />*****Spoilers*****<br /><br />What an amazing tale! Watching Kaylin grow is fantastic, her interactions with the world and people in it is always a surprise. So much happens in this book, it's hard to focus on a few things but Everly and his paintings have become a source of fact when the Oracular Halls are not well respected, the child is. I hope as he grows, they're able to balance his physical needs with the absorption caused by his art by way of his visions.<br /><br />Marcus has taken a back seat and so has the Hawklord as Kaylin interacts more with the Imperial Palace. Hey intuition is incredible and great things happen when she listens to herself. The Devourer turned the Maker in Kaylin's eyes is intriguing and I'm hopeful she'll be able to communicate with him and the elements more frequently in future.<br /><br />Severn has been a silent shadow for most of these books, steadily backing Kaylin however she needs. But he's also somewhat diminished by that role, that is until this book where his love for her saved Kaylin from being consumed by the Devourer. <br /><br />The refugees have a new home in Tiamaris and are ready and willing to face the Shadows. I'd almost forgotten about the outcaste dragon until his roar of challenge. <br /><br />I enjoyed Kaylin's sojourn to the Arkon's hoard mirror because it was impressive and necessary. I also like the Arkon who has more patience than written as well. I'm mostly now looking forward to Kaylin's introduction to the emperor, it's bound to be interesting.<br /><br />The couple of things I don't quite get with these books is that Kaylin rarely seems to bathe. Perhaps the author forgets to mention when it occurs but it's a striking lack. She's doing better now but Kaylin also used to rarely eat which sustaining herself on very little with the feats she undertakes can't last. I was a little confused too, Kaylin's reaction and interaction with Nightshade though his intent is now clear. I think Kaylin should use a little less caution and visit the castle more for many reasons, we'll see what happens though.</span>

  <span id="freeText15763611762555148509" style="display:none">2.5 stars. Once or twice a year I get the urge to return to Elantra, the fantasy city inexplicably named for a mid-priced car. <div id="review_115320270" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115320270" />
    <a title="Amélie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4111736-am-lie"><img alt="Amélie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306018539p2/4111736.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115320270?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amélie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amélie" href="/user/show/4111736-am-lie">Amélie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111736-am-lie?shelf=a-michelle-sagara-west">a-michelle-sagara-west</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111736-am-lie?shelf=c-fantasy">c-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111736-am-lie?shelf=t-romantic">t-romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111736-am-lie?shelf=o-favorites">o-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111736-am-lie?shelf=t-witch-and-wizard">t-witch-and-wizard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111736-am-lie?shelf=t-dragon">t-dragon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115320270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18328572430467997574">Review first published at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://fansofmsw.com/'>http://fansofmsw.com/</a><br/><br/><b>Summary:</b><br/><br/>In this book, the magic in Elani street, the street of the magicians and charlatans, is going wild and the city is threatened by an invasion from another world; Kaylin and Severn are send to investigate this.<br/><br/><b>My opinion:</b><br/><br/>In this book, the relationship between Kaylin, Severn and Nightshade finally progress! Unfortunately, it’s limited to Severn and Nightshade “expressing” their desire/ love for Kaylin and her being uncomfortable about it. Yet i</span>
  <span id="freeText18328572430467997574" style="display:none">Review first published at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://fansofmsw.com/">http://fansofmsw.com/</a><br /><br /><b>Summary:</b><br /><br />In this book, the magic in Elani street, the street of the magicians and charlatans, is going wild and the city is threatened by an invasion from another world; Kaylin and Severn are send to investigate this.<br /><br /><b>My opinion:</b><br /><br />In this book, the relationship between Kaylin, Severn and Nightshade finally progress! Unfortunately, it’s limited to Severn and Nightshade “expressing” their desire/ love for Kaylin and her being uncomfortable about it. Yet it was nice; after all the time I had almost lost all hope… As promise at the end of the last book, we have Nightshade’s reaction to the revelation we get in Silence and we finally learn his motives – or at least part of it, he is Barrani after all. I was rather surprised by part of them (the part about the Regalia) but not disappointed and this revelation promised a change in his behaviour in the future books (though I expected it to come into play before the trip to the West March). It was a pleasant surprise to see him confront Kaylin about her avoiding him and finally kiss her. If Kaylin’s reaction was a little disappointed, it was nonetheless not unexpected considering her past and the trauma she still carries. We also get Severn finally expressing his feeling which was good as I get the impression that if not for the circumstances he would never have done so. Whoever Kaylin end up with (though I obviously hope it will be Nightshade), it is nice that she has to confront their feelings and cannot simply ignore them completely.<br /><br />In this book we also see again Evanton, his garden and the dragons Lords; I was delighted to see more of the Arkon who is as sarcastic as ever and plays a major role in the story; I always appreciate to see the relationship between the dragon Lords.<br /><br />The plot in itself was engrossing and well develop; it was in keeping with the rest of the series, as we see Kaylin use her powers of Chosen to save the world. This book seems to be a sort of complement of Cast in Secret, as we come back to the elemental garden and the elements which I always love to see; we also see again the Oracles (I read this in someone else review, I had personally forgotten about them). Several plot threads which will become relevant for Cast in Peril and Sorrow are also put in place in this book, such as the Consort’s anger at Kaylin for ignoring her “advice”, the egg and the troubles with the Exchequer. I think that the Consort’s anger is well done as it reminds us that the Barrani are not human, or that at last they are powerful immortals in love with political plots: despite all the friendliness she has previously shown Kaylin, the Consort still expects her to obey her and is irrationally angry when she fails to do so. We also meet the Norranir and learn that humans come from another world; I think that it was an interesting development.<br /><br />On the whole, it is a good read essential for the fans of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18328572430467997574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_284666228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/284666228" />
    <a title="Paradoxical" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1964421-paradoxical"><img alt="Paradoxical" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349572735p2/1964421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284666228?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paradoxical" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paradoxical" href="/user/show/1964421-paradoxical">Paradoxical</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1964421-paradoxical?shelf=books-otherwise">books-otherwise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1964421-paradoxical?shelf=2012-reading-list">2012-reading-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284666228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17816620891117772092">This series is, at once, beautiful and frustrating. Sometimes you want to smack Kaylin and sometimes you just want to hug her. If nothing else, the books are entertaining and they capture your attention and imagination very quickly. The author does much the same in <i>Cast in Chaos</i>, expanding and developing the world that she has created and making it something rich and rather lovely (as well as rather terrible to boot).<br/><br/>The beginning of the book was a bit of a mess. It has been a while since I've l</span>
  <span id="freeText17816620891117772092" style="display:none">This series is, at once, beautiful and frustrating. Sometimes you want to smack Kaylin and sometimes you just want to hug her. If nothing else, the books are entertaining and they capture your attention and imagination very quickly. The author does much the same in <i>Cast in Chaos</i>, expanding and developing the world that she has created and making it something rich and rather lovely (as well as rather terrible to boot).<br /><br />The beginning of the book was a bit of a mess. It has been a while since I've last read one of the books, and it was a little confusing and there were names and phrases thrown around like crazy. It's not really a series you can pick up in the middle and expect to figure out everything, but they <i>are</i> standalone, in that each and every book tells a complete story. But once the story gets moving, once you begin to understand a little more, the writing flows out and grasps your attention. More importantly, it holds it, and you're pretty much sucked into the world that is presented before you.<br /><br />The plot of the book is fairly complex and filled with quite of a lot of layers. There is an area in the city that is warped by strange magic--or rather, magic is being warped in the area, and nobody knows why. Kaylin and the rest of the Hawks try to investigate what is happening, and why, with little success until Kaylin, of course, manages to fall out of place in the world and become lost. There is nothing there, and yet there is a presence that terrifies her and she barely manages to escape from such a place. Unfortunately that presence, the Devourer, a being that swallows up worlds, is searching for something, and Kaylin fears that it is her world. And that's just the tip of it, really.<br /><br />The characters are great. Kaylin has grown from what she was in the beginning books, all for the better. She's not as irritating now, she thinks a little more before she jumps into things, but she's still her. She still makes rash decisions and still can't keep her mouth shut for the most part. And, okay, I'm pretty much in love with Nightshade, for no good reason other than I apparently have a certain type in books, and he pretty much encompasses all of it. It's just too bad that he doesn't show up nearly as much as I want him too.<br /><br />But I think what's best about the series is the amount of creativity the author has put into the world. It's a rich, deep, complex world that you can't help but get lost in. It's a little confusing, and sometimes you don't get any answers, but there's always something more and something different. 4 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17816620891117772092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_117494813" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117494813" />
    <a title="Deirdre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4171345-deirdre"><img alt="Deirdre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461881870p2/4171345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117494813?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deirdre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deirdre" href="/user/show/4171345-deirdre">Deirdre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117494813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1069930575691691041">I am impressed. The Chronicles of Elantra series has once again been added to with a fabulous tale. I don't read very much High Fantasy, but these books are too good to pass by! Michelle Sagara does a great job in making sure these novels have a very modern feel, and they are a delight to read. Cast in Chaos, the sixth book, continues the story of the Hawk, (read: law enforcement officer) Kaylin Neya. <br/><br/>Something shifty is going down on the streets of Elantra. More precisely on Elani street. That’</span>
  <span id="freeText1069930575691691041" style="display:none">I am impressed. The Chronicles of Elantra series has once again been added to with a fabulous tale. I don't read very much High Fantasy, but these books are too good to pass by! Michelle Sagara does a great job in making sure these novels have a very modern feel, and they are a delight to read. Cast in Chaos, the sixth book, continues the story of the Hawk, (read: law enforcement officer) Kaylin Neya. <br /><br />Something shifty is going down on the streets of Elantra. More precisely on Elani street. That’s right, the city’s own swindlers row. I mean, really. Hair tonics that actually work and fortunetellers saying something other than, “I see a tall, dark man...”? Unheard of! After it starts raining blood, Kaylin and the Hawks realize something is definitely wrong.<br /><br />When the Oracles reveal that a portal is going to open in the middle of swind- I mean- Elani Street, one that will let in a crowd of tall, pale strangers, all the city is in upset. Now, aside from the stray magic from the portal doing strange things like causing three eyed babies, having new neighbors might not be so bad. Unfortunately, if the portal opens it may let in the being called The Destroyer of Worlds, who would, you guessed it, try to destroy their world. <br /><br />Thanks to freak encounter with The Destroyer, from which she had to be saved by Lord Nightshade, Kaylin is right in the thick of the action. She has to decide, will she try to aid the lost people, or protect those that she loves at any cost?<br /><br />Now, speaking of His Loveliness, The Lord Nightshade... we don’t see nearly enough of him in this book! Take it with a grain of salt though, because I’m always going to want this to turn into a romance, and it is never going to happen. I will say that His Lordship made the time he had in this book count. He does this whole ‘white knight’ thing and, well... *waggles eyebrows*. <br /><br /><br />Kaylin has grown a lot as a character in this series. The evolution has been gradual, and very realistic, over the course of several books. Cast in Chaos does an excellent job furthering her development and spinning a wickedly interesting story. I’m looking forward the next installment, Cast in Ruins, which comes out next year.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1069930575691691041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=class">class</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=sff">sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/617334-madeline?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>,
