          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234969872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4089010089627304131">I mostly find these books diverting, and I usually forget exactly what happens in them pretty soon after I finish each of them. This is kind of inconvenient, since although the books are largely self-contained there are some callbacks to others in the series, and I've forgotten some of the characters. (Also, I seem to have skipped an important book for Tiamaris, my favorite secondary character. Which is just SOP when reading Sagara West books, frankly.) However, I do admire how thematically tigh</span>
  <span id="freeText4089010089627304131" style="display:none">I mostly find these books diverting, and I usually forget exactly what happens in them pretty soon after I finish each of them. This is kind of inconvenient, since although the books are largely self-contained there are some callbacks to others in the series, and I've forgotten some of the characters. (Also, I seem to have skipped an important book for Tiamaris, my favorite secondary character. Which is just SOP when reading Sagara West books, frankly.) However, I do admire how thematically tight they are, and I always enjoy them. The main character is the kind of grumpy, underslept, overworked, frazzled public servant I often enjoy spending time with (Discworld/<i>The West Wing</i>/<i>Southland</i>/<i>Veep</i>), thrust in over her head despite her best efforts to stay under the radar. They read a bit like a cross between <i>Buffy the Vampire Slayer</i> and one of Pratchett's Watch books: they solve crime and save the world! I hope some day we'll get something a bit more . . . domestic, and less apocalyptic, because I think the characters can stand it.<br /><br /><blockquote>"When all of this is over - if we're still alive - I want a vacation."<br />He smiled. "If you consider lessons with members of the Imperial Court a vacation, I'm sure Marcus will be happy to sign off on it."<br />"I could probably get around Sannabalis."<br />"True."<br />It wasn't Sanabalis he was thinking about. "I don't suppose a mouse could get around Diarmat."<br />"<i>Lord</i> Diarmat, and no, not if his reputation is anything to go by. Are you ready?"<br />"No, I never am. I just make do."</blockquote><br /><br />I don't really care about the love triangle because . . . I almost never care about love triangles. But it's kind of mildly interesting in this book, maybe because although people <i>talk about their feelings</i> a lot more, the actual love triangle takes a definite back seat to the end of the world. (As it ought to.)<br /><br />Also, at some point I decided Sanabalis was Werner Herzog. This definitely makes reading the book and his lines more fun. It's a strategy I'll be adopting more often in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4089010089627304131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1565095483" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Elizabeth Glew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6319068-elizabeth-glew"><img alt="Elizabeth Glew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316118802p2/6319068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1565095483?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Glew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Glew" href="/user/show/6319068-elizabeth-glew">Elizabeth Glew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8698700-cast-in-chaos">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1565095483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9309935280997511851">I wish I could review the series instead of individual books. Since I haven't figured out how to do that, I am posting this review for each of the six books I have read. I picked up this series to pass the time while recovering from a back injury, and it's okay for that purpose. The quality of writing is it exactly what one should expect from a Harlequin publication: just adequate, not at all elegant. Each book has two or three really good snippets, but these are outweighed by the difficulty of </span>
  <span id="freeText9309935280997511851" style="display:none">I wish I could review the series instead of individual books. Since I haven't figured out how to do that, I am posting this review for each of the six books I have read. I picked up this series to pass the time while recovering from a back injury, and it's okay for that purpose. The quality of writing is it exactly what one should expect from a Harlequin publication: just adequate, not at all elegant. Each book has two or three really good snippets, but these are outweighed by the difficulty of following most of the dialogue. It is almost always hard to figure out who is speaking.<br /><br /> The plots are entertaining, but development of both the characters and their environment is sadly lacking. The author seems to have very few original ideas, and draws heavily on the work of earlier masters of the genre, most notably McCaffrey and Le Guin. Her best creation, in my opinion, is a race of sentient, humanoid lions, but even these lack depth. <br /><br />Every author of fantasy relies on her readers' suspension of disbelief, but Sagara stretches that capacity beyond its limits with many of the situations she creates. A character who is presented as the best teacher on the planet persists, for years, in setting our heroine the same task she has repeatedly failed with every previous teacher. The head midwife abruptly dumps her most difficult problem in the lap of an untrained, 20-year-old, low-ranking police officer. A possessive, fire breathing dragon is conveniently called away on an errand, leaving our heroine alone with some of the most valuable objects in his hoard.<br /><br />Think of Tolkien's works as fine, aged cheese. These books are Cheetos.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9309935280997511851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11392097813745640928">The problem with this book is its too long. As you know from reading the Kaylin books previously, Kaylin, who is a lowly Private in the Hawks, which are guards and detectives for the Empire, also happens to have been blessed or cursed with magical sigils and runes that are affixed all over her body. She is a Chosen, and through her magic has in previous books, healed the Barrani, an immortal race of beings who needed her gifts as the Chosen and as a midwife to save their Prince and Queen.<br/>In this</span>
  <span id="freeText11392097813745640928" style="display:none">The problem with this book is its too long. As you know from reading the Kaylin books previously, Kaylin, who is a lowly Private in the Hawks, which are guards and detectives for the Empire, also happens to have been blessed or cursed with magical sigils and runes that are affixed all over her body. She is a Chosen, and through her magic has in previous books, healed the Barrani, an immortal race of beings who needed her gifts as the Chosen and as a midwife to save their Prince and Queen.<br />In this overlong saga in the same world, Kaylin learns that a mysterious destroyer of worlds, known only as the Devourer is journeying towards her Empire and world.<br /><br />Sagara reference yet again the same group of characters from her other book - Sanbalis the dragon mage, Arkon, the dragon librarian, the Keeper of the Elemental Garden, Tiamaris, a dragon who is now a Fief Lord etc.<br /><br />There is nothing super new in this book, most of the same players are present and the denouement, is essentially obvious from the beginning.<br /><br />The best of these books, when Kaylin uses her powers to heal or help right a wrong are moving and you can over look some annoying facts, but this book, where Kaylin rights a wrong done to a godlike being, seems to me to be too pat, too predictable, and especially too long.<br /><br /> <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText9926731673188917236" style="display:none">Oh my there is only one more to reread....(T_T)<br /><br />After rereading this book I realized that it has one of the most heart-warming confessions of the series.   <span id="freeText15801978941370954795" style="display:none">Someone else calls this "The Book in Which People's Questions Are [finally] Answered." She's not wrong. With a re-reading or two, this might make it up to my second favorite in the series. (My favorite is still Cast in Courtlight.) I'm still enjoying the series, and especially enjoying the idea that Kaylin has to learn from her mistakes, and that she is winning through by guess and golly just as much as any skills she may acquire. I start out really enjoying the story, the plot, the world, the characters, etc. But then the climax hits and things get much too wordy over the metaphysical stuff, at which point I start skimming lots and lots. I also wish Sagara would switch things up a bit. I would love to see Kaylin partnered up with Teela, Tain, and Clint instead of Severn all the time. And there are only so many end of the world scenarios that one can take before it gets</span>
  <span id="freeText1483897839221886733" style="display:none">Well, I think I'm noticing a trend with these books. I start out really enjoying the story, the plot, the world, the characters, etc. But then the climax hits and things get much too wordy over the metaphysical stuff, at which point I start skimming lots and lots. I also wish Sagara would switch things up a bit. I would love to see Kaylin partnered up with Teela, Tain, and Clint instead of Severn all the time. And there are only so many end of the world scenarios that one can take before it gets old. I'll likely finish off the series as it gets completed, but it does seem to be dragging along. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sgWjqSER1c6WyCzZTvhxo5oK0+eopggaknGk9OrUeDW+5S2zRB6p+b0JujaqhhtSkZv7KzXEuwVn7I4pj1OGtQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
